'To solve the equation \n\n\\[\n\\arctan \\frac{1}{x} + \\arctan \\frac{1}{x + 2} = \\arctan \\frac{4}{x + 3},\n\\]\n\nwe can use the tangent addition formula for arctan, which states that if \\(\\arctan a + \\arctan b = \\arctan c\\), then\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a + b}{1 - ab} = c.\n\\]\n\nApplying this to our equation, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\frac{1}{x} + \\frac{1}{x+2}}{1 - \\frac{1}{x} \\cdot \\frac{1}{x+2}} = \\frac{4}{x+3}.\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the left-hand side:\n\n1. The numerator is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{x} + \\frac{1}{x+2} = \\frac{x+2 + x}{x(x+2)} = \\frac{2x+2}{x(x+2)} = \\frac{2(x+1)}{x(x+2)}.\n\\]\n\n2. The denominator is:\n\n\\[\n1 - \\frac{1}{x} \\cdot \\frac{1}{x+2} = 1 - \\frac{1}{x(x+2)} = \\frac{x(x+2) - 1}{x(x+2)} = \\frac{x^2 + 2x - 1}{x(x+2)}.\n\\]\n\nThus, the left-hand side becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\frac{2(x+1)}{x(x+2)}}{\\frac{x^2 + 2x - 1}{x(x+2)}} = \\frac{2(x+1)}{x^2 + 2x - 1}.\n\\]\n\nEquating this to the right-hand side:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2(x+1)}{x^2 + 2x - 1} = \\frac{4}{x+3}.\n\\]\n\nCross-multiplying gives:\n\n\\[\n2(x+1)(x+3) = 4(x^2 + 2x - 1).\n\\]\n\nExpanding both sides:\n\n- Left-hand side: \\(2(x+1)(x+3) = 2(x^2 + 3x + x + 3) = 2(x^2 + 4x + 3) = 2x^2 + 8x + 6\\).\n- Right-hand side: \\(4(x^2 + 2x - 1) = 4x^2 + 8x - 4\\).\n\nSetting them equal:\n\n\\[\n2x^2 + 8x + 6 = 4x^2 + 8x - 4.\n\\]\n\nSubtract \\(2x^2 + 8x + 6\\) from both sides:\n\n\\[\n0 = 2x^2 - 10.\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n2x^2 = 10 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x^2 = 5 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x = \\pm \\sqrt{5}.\n\\]\n\nThus, the solutions are:\n\n1. \\(x = \\sqrt{5}\\)\n2. \\(x = -\\sqrt{5}\\)'

'1. **Matrix Multiplication Process:** To find the product of two matrices, take the dot product of the rows of the first matrix with the columns of the second matrix.\n\n2. **Resulting Matrix Size:** The product of two 2x2 matrices is another 2x2 matrix.\n\n3. **First Row, First Column Calculation:**\n   \\[\n   (3a^2 - 3)(-1) + (3a)(a) = 3\n   \\]\n\n4. **First Row, Second Column Calculation:**\n   \\[\n   (3a^2 - 3)(-3a - 2) + (3a)(3a^2 + 2a - 3) = 12a^2 - 6\n   \\]\n\n5. **Second Row, First Column Calculation:**\n   \\[\n   (2a^2 - a - 2)(-1) + (2a - 1)(a) = 2\n   \\]\n\n6. **Second Row, Second Column Calculation:**\n   \\[\n   (2a^2 - a - 2)(-3a - 2) + (2a - 1)(3a^2 + 2a - 3) = 6a^2 + 1\n   \\]\n\n7. **Final Resulting Matrix:**\n   \\[\n   \\begin{pmatrix} 3 & 12a^2 - 6 \\\\ 2 & 6a^2 + 1 \\end{pmatrix}\n   \\]'
'To solve the equation, we need to simplify the left-hand side:\n\n1. The expression inside the parentheses is a sum of sines of angles in an arithmetic progression: \\(\\sin 2\\theta + \\sin 4\\theta + \\sin 6\\theta + \\cdots + \\sin 14\\theta\\).\n\n2. This sum can be simplified using the formula for the sum of a sine series: \n   \\[\n   \\sum_{k=1}^{n} \\sin(a + (k-1)d) = \\frac{\\sin\\left(\\frac{nd}{2}\\right)}{\\sin\\left(\\frac{d}{2}\\right)} \\sin\\left(a + \\frac{(n-1)d}{2}\\right)\n   \\]\n   where \\(a = 2\\theta\\), \\(d = 2\\theta\\), and \\(n = 7\\).\n\n3. Applying the formula, the sum becomes:\n   \\[\n   \\sin 2\\theta + \\sin 4\\theta + \\sin 6\\theta + \\cdots + \\sin 14\\theta = \\frac{\\sin(7\\theta)}{\\sin(\\theta)} \\sin(8\\theta)\n   \\]\n\n4. The left-hand side of the original equation becomes:\n   \\[\n   2 \\sin \\theta \\cdot \\frac{\\sin(7\\theta)}{\\sin(\\theta)} \\sin(8\\theta) = 2 \\sin(7\\theta) \\sin(8\\theta)\n   \\]\n\n5. Pythagorean identity: \\(\\sin^2 \\theta + \\cos^2 \\theta = 1\\).\n\n6. Substitution into identity: \\((\\cos^2 \\theta)^2 + \\cos^2 \\theta = 1\\).\n\n7. Let \\(x = \\cos^2 \\theta\\), resulting in: \\(x^2 + x - 1 = 0\\).\n\n8. Solve quadratic equation: \\(x = \\frac{-1 \\pm \\sqrt{5}}{2}\\).\n\n9. Non-negative solution: \\(x = \\frac{-1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2}\\).\n\n10. \\(\\cos^2 \\theta = \\frac{-1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2}\\).\n\n11. \\(\\sin \\theta = \\cos^2 \\theta = \\frac{-1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2}\\).\n\n12. Expression to evaluate: \\(\\frac{1 + \\sin \\theta}{1 - \\sin \\theta} - \\frac{1 - \\sin \\theta}{1 + \\sin \\theta}\\).\n\n13. Simplification: \\(\\frac{a^2 - b^2}{ab}\\) where \\(a = 1 + \\sin \\theta\\) and \\(b = 1 - \\sin \\theta\\).\n\n14. \\(a^2 - b^2 = 4\\sin \\theta\\).\n\n15. \\(ab = \\cos^2 \\theta\\).\n\n16. Final expression: \\(\\frac{4\\sin \\theta}{\\cos^2 \\theta} = 4\\).\n\n17. Result: The value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{4}\\).'

The sum of the roots \\( u + v + w = 0 \\) for the equation \\( z^3 - 1 = 0 \\).\n3. The product of the roots taken two at a time, \\( uv + uw + vw \\), can be found using the identity for the sum of products of roots taken two at a time: \\( uv + uw + vw = (u+v+w)^2 - (u^2 + v^2 + w^2) \\).\n4. Since \\( u = 1 \\), \\( v = \\omega \\), and \\( w = \\omega^2 \\), we have \\( u^2 + v^2 + w^2 = 1^2 + \\omega^2 + (\\omega^2)^2 = 1 + \\omega^2 + \\omega^4 = 1 + \\omega^2 + \\omega = 0 \\) because \\( \\omega^3 = 1 \\) and \\( \\omega^2 + \\omega + 1 = 0 \\).\n5. The domain of the function \\(\\arcsin x\\) is \\([-1, 1]\\).\n\n4. The function \\(f(x) = \\arctan x + \\frac{1}{2} \\arcsin x\\) is defined for all \\(x \\in \\mathbb{R}\\) because \\(\\arctan x\\) is defined for all real numbers, and \\(\\arcsin x\\) is defined for \\(x \\in [-1, 1]\\).\n\n5. For \\(x \\in [-1, 1]\\), the function \\(f(x)\\) is a sum of \\(\\arctan x\\) and \\(\\frac{1}{2} \\arcsin x\\).\n\n6. '1. **Symmetry Property of Tangent Function**: The tangent function has the property that \\(\\tan(90^\\circ - \\theta) = \\cot \\theta\\).\n\n2. **Complementary Angles**: For angles that are complementary, such as \\(10^\\circ\\) and \\(80^\\circ\\), \\(20^\\circ\\) and \\(70^\\circ\\), \\(30^\\circ\\) and \\(60^\\circ\\), and \\(40^\\circ\\) and \\(50^\\circ\\), the product of their tangents is 1 because \\(\\tan \\theta \\cdot \\tan(90^\\circ - \\theta) = 1\\).\n\n3. **Specific Values**: \n   - \\(\\tan 30^\\circ = \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{3}}\\)\n   - \\(\\tan 60^\\circ = \\sqrt{3}\\)\n\n4. **Product Simplification**: Using the symmetry property and complementary angles, the product simplifies as follows:\n   \\[\n   \\tan 10^\\circ \\tan 80^\\circ = 1, \\quad \\tan 20^\\circ \\tan 70^\\circ = 1, \\quad \\tan 30^\\circ \\tan 60^\\circ = 1, \\quad \\tan 40^\\circ \\tan 50^\\circ = 1\n   \\]\n\n5. **Final Product**: The entire product \\(\\tan 10^\\circ \\tan 20^\\circ \\tan 30^\\circ \\tan 40^\\circ \\tan 50^\\circ \\tan 60^\\circ \\tan 70^\\circ \\tan 80^\\circ\\) simplifies to \\(1 \\times 1 \\times 1 \\times 1 = 1\\).'
'1. Given equation: \\(\\frac{\\cos \\alpha}{\\cos \\beta} + \\frac{\\sin \\alpha}{\\sin \\beta} = -1\\).\n\n2. Set \\( x = \\frac{\\cos \\alpha}{\\cos \\beta} \\) and \\( y = \\frac{\\sin \\alpha}{\\sin \\beta} \\), leading to \\( x + y = -1 \\).\n\n3. Expression to find: \\(\\frac{\\cos^3 \\beta}{\\cos \\alpha} + \\frac{\\sin^3 \\beta}{\\sin \\alpha}\\).\n\n4. Substitute: \\(\\frac{\\cos^3 \\beta}{\\cos \\alpha} = \\frac{1}{x} \\cos^2 \\beta\\) and \\(\\frac{\\sin^3 \\beta}{\\sin \\alpha} = \\frac{1}{y} \\sin^2 \\beta\\).\n\n5. Use identity: \\(\\cos^2 \\beta + \\sin^2 \\beta = 1\\).\n\n6. Expression becomes: \\(\\frac{\\cos^2 \\beta}{x} + \\frac{\\sin^2 \\beta}{y} = \\frac{\\cos^2 \\beta y + \\sin^2 \\beta x}{xy}\\).\n\n7. Use identity: \\(\\sin^2 \\beta - \\cos^2 \\beta = -\\cos 2\\beta\\).\n\n10. Expression simplifies to: \\(\\frac{-\\cos^2 \\beta - x \\cos 2\\beta}{x(-1-x)}\\).\n\n11. Final result: The value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
'1. Use the sum-to-product identities for sine: \\(\\sin A + \\sin B = 2 \\sin \\left( \\frac{A+B}{2} \\right) \\cos \\left( \\frac{A-B}{2} \\right)\\).\n\n2. Apply the identity to \\(\\sin 17^\\circ + \\sin 43^\\circ\\):\n   - \\(A = 17^\\circ\\), \\(B = 43^\\circ\\).\n   - \\(\\frac{A+B}{2} = \\frac{17^\\circ + 43^\\circ}{2} = 30^\\circ\\).\n   - \\(\\frac{A-B}{2} = \\frac{17^\\circ - 43^\\circ}{2} = -13^\\circ\\).\n\n3. Simplify using the identity:\n   - \\(\\sin 17^\\circ + \\sin 43^\\circ = 2 \\sin 30^\\circ \\cos (-13^\\circ)\\).\n\n4. Use the fact that \\(\\cos(-\\theta) = \\cos(\\theta)\\):\n   - \\(\\cos(-13^\\circ) = \\cos(13^\\circ)\\).\n\n5. Simplify further:\n   - \\(\\sin 17^\\circ + \\sin 43^\\circ = 2 \\sin 30^\\circ \\cos 13^\\circ\\).\n\n6. Since \\(\\sin 30^\\circ = \\frac{1}{2}\\), the expression becomes:\n   - \\(2 \\times \\frac{1}{2} \\times \\cos 13^\\circ = \\cos 13^\\circ\\).\n\n7. The simplified expression is \\(\\cos 13^\\circ\\).'
'To find the normal vector of the plane \\( P \\) through which the given matrix reflects, we need to understand that the reflection matrix \\( R \\) is given by:\n\n1. **Reflection Matrix Formula**: \n   \\[\n   R = I - 2 \\mathbf{n} \\mathbf{n}^T\n   \\]\n   where \\( \\mathbf{n} \\) is the unit normal vector to the plane, and \\( I \\) is the identity matrix.\n\n2. **Given Reflection Matrix**:\n   \\[\n   R = \\begin{pmatrix} \\frac{11}{15} & \\frac{2}{15} & \\frac{2}{3} \\\\ \\frac{2}{15} & \\frac{14}{15} & -\\frac{1}{3} \\\\ \\frac{2}{3} & -\\frac{1}{3} & -\\frac{2}{3} \\end{pmatrix}\n   \\]\n\n3. **Calculate \\( I - R \\)**:\n   \\[\n   I = \\begin{pmatrix} 1 & 0 & 0 \\\\ 0 & 1 & 0 \\\\ 0 & 0 & 1 \\end{pmatrix}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   I - R = \\begin{pmatrix} \\frac{4}{15} & -\\frac{2}{15} & -\\frac{2}{3} \\\\ -\\frac{2}{15} & \\frac{1}{15} & \\frac{1}{3} \\\\ -\\frac{2}{3} & \\frac{1}{3} & \\frac{5}{3} \\end{pmatrix}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Relate to Normal Vector**:\n   \\[\n   2 \\mathbf{n} \\mathbf{n}^T = \\begin{pmatrix} \\frac{4}{15} & -\\frac{2}{15} & -\\frac{2}{3} \\\\ -\\frac{2}{15} & \\frac{1}{15} & \\frac{1}{3} \\\\ -\\frac{2}{3} & \\frac{1}{3} & \\frac{5}{3} \\end{pmatrix}\n   \\]\n\n5. **Diagonal Elements**:\n   - \\( 2n_1^2 = \\frac{4}{15} \\)\n   - \\( 2n_2^2 = \\frac{1}{15} \\)\n   - \\( 2n_3^2 = \\frac{5}{3} \\)\n\n6. **Solve for \\( n_1, n_2, n_3 \\)**:\n   - \\( n_1^2 = \\frac{2}{15} \\)\n   - \\( n_2^2 = \\frac{1}{30} \\)\n   - \\( n_3^2 = \\frac{5}{6} \\)\n\n7. **Normal Vector in Integer Form**:\n   - Proportional to:\n     \\[\n     \\begin{pmatrix} \\sqrt{2} \\\\ \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{2}} \\\\ \\sqrt{5} \\end{pmatrix}\n     \\]\n   - Integer form:\n     \\[\n     \\begin{pmatrix} 2 \\\\ 1 \\\\ 5 \\end{pmatrix}\n     \\]\n\n8. **Final Answer**:\n   - The normal vector of the plane \\( P \\) is:\n     \\[\n     \\boxed{\\begin{pmatrix} 2 \\\\ 1 \\\\ 5 \\end{pmatrix}}\n     \\]'

'1. The formula for the cosine of the angle \\(\\theta\\) between two vectors \\(\\mathbf{a}\\) and \\(\\mathbf{b}\\) is \\(\\cos \\theta = \\frac{\\mathbf{a} \\cdot \\mathbf{b}}{\\|\\mathbf{a}\\| \\|\\mathbf{b}\\|}\\).\n\n2. The dot product \\(\\mathbf{a} \\cdot \\mathbf{b}\\) is calculated as \\(4 \\cdot 1 + 4 \\cdot 4 + 7 \\cdot 1 = 27\\).\n\n3. The magnitude of vector \\(\\mathbf{a} = \\begin{pmatrix} 4 \\\\ 4 \\\\ 7 \\end{pmatrix}\\) is \\(\\|\\mathbf{a}\\| = 9\\).\n\n4. The magnitude of vector \\(\\mathbf{b} = \\begin{pmatrix} 1 \\\\ 4 \\\\ 1 \\end{pmatrix}\\) is \\(\\|\\mathbf{b}\\| = 3\\sqrt{2}\\).\n\n5. Substituting into the cosine formula gives \\(\\cos \\theta = \\frac{27}{27\\sqrt{2}} = \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{2}} = \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2}\\).\n\n6. The angle \\(\\theta\\) whose cosine is \\(\\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2}\\) is \\(45^\\circ\\).\n\n7. Therefore, the angle between the vectors is \\(45^\\circ\\).'
